A comparative study was conducted comprising a protected area in Kibale National Park and surrounding farmlands to establish how farmlands mimic the forest floristic structure. Study results show very low similarity between the forest and farmland ecosystems (<mml:math xmlns:mml=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\" id=\"M1\"><mml:mrow><mml:mi>C</mml:mi><mml:msub><mml:mi>C</mml:mi><mml:mi>j</mml:mi></mml:msub><mml:mo>=</mml:mo><mml:mn>0.11</mml:mn></mml:mrow></mml:math>). A total of 50 and 29 species were identified in the forest and, farmland, respectively; 8 were shared. Importance value indices of woody species in the forest ranged from 0.3 to 29.9 with <jats:italic>Celtis durandii</jats:italic> being the most important while those in the farmland were 1.9\u201379.2, <jats:italic>Eucalyptus grandis</jats:italic>, having the highest index. Woody species diversity and evenness were higher in the forest ecosystem (<mml:math xmlns:mml=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\" id=\"M2\"><mml:mrow><mml:msup><mml:mi>H</mml:mi><mml:mo>\u2032</mml:mo></mml:msup><mml:mo>=</mml:mo><mml:mn>3.46</mml:mn></mml:mrow></mml:math>, <mml:math xmlns:mml=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\" id=\"M3\"><mml:mrow><mml:msup><mml:mi>J</mml:mi><mml:mo>\u2032</mml:mo></mml:msup><mml:mo>=</mml:mo><mml:mn>0.85</mml:mn></mml:mrow></mml:math>) compared to the farmland (<mml:math xmlns:mml=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\" id=\"M4\"><mml:mrow><mml:msup><mml:mi>H</mml:mi><mml:mo>\u2032</mml:mo></mml:msup><mml:mo>=</mml:mo><mml:mn>2.72</mml:mn></mml:mrow></mml:math>, <mml:math xmlns:mml=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\" id=\"M5\"><mml:mrow><mml:msup><mml:mi>J</mml:mi><mml:mo>\u2032</mml:mo></mml:msup><mml:mo>=</mml:mo><mml:mn>0.79</mml:mn></mml:mrow></mml:math>). The 10\u2013&lt;20\u2009cm diameter class was the lowest in both ecosystems. Communities adjacent to the park should be educated about the value of the park and conservation in general. Since adjacent farmlands provide important ecotones to the park, on-farm indigenous tree retention and planting are required.
